  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3a0b34b1-8df3-440d-ae86-a3f123e94f06'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText7259115246202215021" style="display:none">A new chapter is opened in the Sohma family's story--and the rumors are true! Kyo has indeed met Kyoko in the past...and when he did, she told him the story of how she met Tohru's father, which he then tells to us: Tohru's birth...the truth about her mother and father...Yuki's declaration of independence...<br /><br />Grab your best friend and get ready for the New Year's Eve Ball--everything you've been waiting to know is right inside the next volume of the super-popular <i>Fruits Basket</i>, the world's #1 shojo manga!</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2746447477" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2746447477" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2746447477?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783551769763" href="/book/show/7954064-fruits-basket-vol-16">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2746447477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2052216708746781629">I love this manga so, so, so damn much! The relationships, the way people take care of each other, the gentle gestures. Just everything, really. Fruits Basket is definitely one of the best mangas I ever read and I don’t want it to end. >_< Jeez! This volume was so emotional! <br/><br/><u>
  <b>Thoughts to the highlights of this volume:</b>
</u><br/><br/>- I had absolutely <b>NO IDEA</b> how Tohru’s parents got to know each other and therefore soaked up their background story like a sponge! Those two!! GAH! I love them! They were such a</span>
  <span id="freeText2052216708746781629" style="display:none">I love this manga so, so, so damn much! The relationships, the way people take care of each other, the gentle gestures. Just everything, really. Fruits Basket is definitely one of the best mangas I ever read and I don’t want it to end. &gt;_&lt; Jeez! This volume was so emotional! <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Thoughts to the highlights of this volume:</b>
</u><br /><br />- I had absolutely <b>NO IDEA</b> how Tohru’s parents got to know each other and therefore soaked up their background story like a sponge! Those two!! GAH! I love them! They were such an unconventional couple! My favourite part of their first meeting: Katsuya seeing right through her anger and stating that she just wants to be loved. T_T<br /><br />- <b>THAT SUPER CASUAL MARRIAGE PROPOSAL!!!!</b> Excuse me while I die! &lt;333 <br /><br />- The death of Tohru’s father and how broken her mother was. I could relate so much and my heart broke for her. AND I was in tears when Kyoko remembered that she has someone to live for. Little Tohru... T_T <br /><br />- Yuki and Machi!!!! &lt;333 <b>I. SHIP. IT.!!!</b> I love that he notices her and that she’s so flustered because he pays attention to everything she says or does! If things continue like that I might ship them even more than I ship Kyo and Tohru and that says quite something! <br /><br />- Haru and Rin! He’s so gentle and tender with her. Gosh, he loves her so much it already hurt to see him touch her face while she was asleep. I really hope there will come a day when they can be together. <br /><br />- Akito needs to get out of the way. Seriously! What he did to Yuki just because he told him the truth and forgave him? I really dislike him more and more! *grrrrr*</span>
  <a data-text-id="2052216708746781629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_178174000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178174000" />
    <a title="Rain Misoa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4481312-rain-misoa"><img alt="Rain Misoa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305629680p2/4481312.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178174000?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rain Misoa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rain Misoa" href="/user/show/4481312-rain-misoa">Rain Misoa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE!!! And anyone who loves seeing Mommy and Daddy together~</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rain by: </span>
      Nicole Terazue
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4481312-rain-misoa?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178174000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16868166028488658794">*Gets a spork, goes to the Corner of Woe, and begins hacking away* (Don't try this at home, kids!) My God! What a depressing volume! I was emo throughout most of it... IF NOT ALL!!! This book centers around Kyoko and let me tell you, it's going to make you want to sit down in front of the TV screen watching mediocre shows with a big bucket of ice cream, cookies, and donuts on top! It's just THAT depressing. Not to mention, once you get pass Kyoko's story, you get the sadness from Machi's story. </span>
  <span id="freeText16868166028488658794" style="display:none">*Gets a spork, goes to the Corner of Woe, and begins hacking away* (Don't try this at home, kids!) My God! What a depressing volume! I was emo throughout most of it... IF NOT ALL!!! This book centers around Kyoko and let me tell you, it's going to make you want to sit down in front of the TV screen watching mediocre shows with a big bucket of ice cream, cookies, and donuts on top! It's just THAT depressing. Not to mention, once you get pass Kyoko's story, you get the sadness from Machi's story. And if THAT'S not enough, you then get Akito thrown in your face! So it's like, sad, sad, then BOOM! You're pissed off because of the asswipe! -_-" Can I kick someone? Please? It'll make me feel so much better. I need to feel better right now because I'm just about ready to throw someone into traffic. Ugh! So... blah!!! I've never felt more depressed or pissed in my life! (I have. I just like being over-dramatic. X3) Man, this is awesome! I love things that can make me so upset! It shows just how awesome something really is! XD<br /><br />Sensei, you are my love! I love you! Te amo! Je t'aime! Daisuki! And all them other ones that means you are sexy and I think you are amazing. Seriously, Takaya-sensei keeps throwing things together so well that it adds so much to the DRAMA! This is some good drama! Whoo! *Sugar High* Totally making pancakes after this! X3 Anyway, where was I...? Um... oh yeah! I love how she creates back story! I love learning about these wonderful characters and the fact that this one focused more on Kyoko, well, it just made it that much more epic. If you thought you knew everything there is to know about Kyoko then think again. Man, that story was so engaging (and sad) that I was literally eating it up as if it were pancakes! (Man... I'm really craving pancakes.) This mangaka is amazing! I can't stress it enough. And I do love her clothing designs for Rin! That girl can dress! I wish I had access to clothes like that but... I live in the middle of nowhere so it's hard to find. Nothing like online shopping, ne? ^_^ Takaya-sensei, keep doing a wonderful job!<br /><br />Kyoko and Katsuya. Best. Couple. Ever. I'm not joking! They just have such a wonderful relationship together. We all know how badass Kyoko was. We've been seeing bits and pieces of her throughout the entire manga. But this is the first time we have fully seen how sexy Katsuya, Tohru's father, was! I love how he's not exactly very gentle. Yeah, he just goes up and says it how it is. I love that in people. It's amazing! (Not sure how to take his lolita complex. XD) My favorite part of him is how he takes insults as compliments and it pisses Kyoko off. It's hilarious! They are just so cute together so when you see the tragic stuff, it hurts all the more. Her story hurt me just as much as Kyo's did. *Sighs* I love these characters. Another part of the story that made me sad was Machi. We see more of why she acts so strangely. It's, of course, the circumstances that her life has her in. Seeing her feel useless was... unsettling. But it helps you grasp her situation a bit better. She does seem to be changing herself, though. Especially when it comes to Yuki. He seems to be helping her a lot even if it's very subtle at the moment. <br /><br />Last part I want to talk about... AKITO! DAMN THAT BLOODY NO GOOD FU--*Insert various curse words here* I can't stand him! How can anyone!? I don't know how they do it but please, let me in on your secret! I don't think I can handle him for much longer! He's so evil! He went--no. I can't say it! But it was another thing that makes me want to burn him alive! You think that he would be a little more... oh, I don't know... CIVILIZED!!! Ack! I have a headache. I needs me some sugar in order calm my nerves. (Where's the bloody pancakes when you need them!?) Whatever! Moving on! Momiji is so adorable. I love how he's always helping Tohru out. Like with what he did with Kureno! That was cute. Kureno better shape up soon or I'm going to kick his ass as well! &gt;_&lt; Kyo has... more secrets than he's telling people but I can't say much about him. It's too spoiler-y. I'm just... concerned. Hmm... anyway... Hatori... looked... so... HOT!!! in that outfit of his! Dude, I think I fell in love with him~ AGAIN! Is that possible? But oh! He had a slip of the tongue! Tee-Hee-Hee!!! X3 On a final note, Haru is so wonderful. So gentle. Hold me, darling! I'll please you in more ways than on--*Gets shot* ...I really need to find the ass who keeps doing that. -_-"<br /><br />Despite the fact that I went insane (again) in this volume, I really did enjoy myself. Getting to know Katsuya and Kyoko more was very nice. The bit with Machi was also nice. And just seeing all of the other characters growing into something much more than they already are is always something I am willing to accept! I want to see more and I cannot wait to get into the next volume! Do yourself a favor and read, man! Read till your heart explodes from all the cute, depressing, wonderful, agonizing, amazing content of this series. *Dreamy sigh* I wants me a Hatori. No. Haru. No. Kyo. No... SOHMA! (Minus asswipe.) Yeah... I'm hooked. This is my crack and I'm sucking it all up! Now, I think I'm going to make me some pancakes because I needs something to calm my nerves before I continue on. I know it's going to contain some of the stupid in the next volume and I can use all the sugar I can get. -_-" Join me after the pancakes! (SHUT UP ALREADY!!!) &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="16868166028488658794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2718251636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2718251636" />
    <a title="Delirious Disquisitions" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5831406-delirious-disquisitions"><img alt="Delirious Disquisitions" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600382655p2/5831406.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2718251636?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Delirious Disquisitions" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Delirious Disquisitions" href="/user/show/5831406-delirious-disquisitions">Delirious Disquisitions</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=manga-manhua-webtoon">manga-manhua-webtoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2718251636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5232049621164153200">I'm going to ignore the fact that Tohru's dad was in his 20s when he fell in love with and married Tohru's mom, a middle school kid. I think my head would burst if I think on it too much so I'm going to pretend they were a couple of years apart. In that light their story was cute but also so very tragic. It was nice to see this flawed and very human version of Tohru's mom since most of the time we only see the perfect version of her that Tohru remembers. She's always on a pedestal that it's hard</span>
  <span id="freeText5232049621164153200" style="display:none">I'm going to ignore the fact that Tohru's dad was in his 20s when he fell in love with and married Tohru's mom, a middle school kid. I think my head would burst if I think on it too much so I'm going to pretend they were a couple of years apart. In that light their story was cute but also so very tragic. It was nice to see this flawed and very human version of Tohru's mom since most of the time we only see the perfect version of her that Tohru remembers. She's always on a pedestal that it's hard fo remember she was also human and had her own struggles in life. <br /><br />Kyou and Tohru's love story is shaping up nicely and the masochist side of me likes that it's going at a snail's pace. A close favourite is Haru and Rin's story with its tragic, Shakespearean undertones. I really do hope they end up happy together. I remain less than convinced about Kureno and Uotani's story. <br /><br />The highlight, as always, is the trio relationship and individual narrative arcs. Yuki seems little more at peace with his feelings for Tohru. He's also slowly healing his psychological scars and learning to love past the trauma; something Akito is obviously not happy with. Kyou's struggles with his feelings for Tohru is slowly coming to a head. It can't be long before he gives in and accepts that they belong together. I wish Tohru would be a little more proactive in searching for ways to break the curse. But she's doing so much already healing everybody and single handedly taking care of her 12+ kids that it's hard to fault her! <br /><br />This volume covers chapters 90-95. <b>4.5 stars.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5232049621164153200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2983189374" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2983189374" />
    <a title="Elizabeth N. | ThePennilessBooknerd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54023065-elizabeth-n-thepennilessbooknerd"><img alt="Elizabeth N. | ThePennilessBooknerd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595397456p2/54023065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2983189374?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth N. | ThePennilessBooknerd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth N. | ThePennilessBooknerd" href="/user/show/54023065-elizabeth-n-thepennilessbooknerd">Elizabeth N. | ThePennilessBooknerd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54023065-elizabeth-n-thepennilessbooknerd?shelf=genre-comics-manga-graphic-novels">genre-comics-manga-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54023065-elizabeth-n-thepennilessbooknerd?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2983189374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6465758876794602648">I’m really torn on how to rate this…<br/>I guess I should just say my thoughts first. So, Tohru’s mom and dad are eight years apart, which that fact by itself isn’t too much of a problem, except for the fact that they met when Kyoko (Tohru’s Mom) was only 14, and in middle school where Katsuya (Tohru’s dad) was a student teacher, and would have been 22… Yeah I had a major problem with this. It feel like an abuse of authority. I understand the story, I get Kyoko was struggling and he helped her, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText6465758876794602648" style="display:none">I’m really torn on how to rate this…<br />I guess I should just say my thoughts first. So, Tohru’s mom and dad are eight years apart, which that fact by itself isn’t too much of a problem, except for the fact that they met when Kyoko (Tohru’s Mom) was only 14, and in middle school where Katsuya (Tohru’s dad) was a student teacher, and would have been 22… Yeah I had a major problem with this. It feel like an abuse of authority. I understand the story, I get Kyoko was struggling and he helped her, but there are so many situations where an adult abuses their power to manipulate a kid who is already struggling, into a relationship with them. Look at the Onision stuff on YouTube for a large example. I know Katsuya isn’t like that and comparing is somewhat wrong, but at the same time it’s not. This is a series aimed at 13 - 16 or so year olds. If someone that age read this and saw this story, they possibly wouldn’t see anything wrong with it. Literally if it was years later, say Kyoko was 18, or even better yet, 20. I wouldn’t have as much of a problem with it that I do now, but I really can’t overlook the age difference and how they met. After I started reading this I put it down for 2 days because I was really weirded out by it. I get that he really cares for Kyoko, but I seriously feel that it is sending a bad message. Am I over analyzing, maybe. Do I care if I am, not really. I feel that this needs to be pointed out. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the last two chapters. Learning more about Machi. She’s still a mystery right now, but I like how Yuki is trying to be her friend. I really hate Akito, but doesn't everyone? Apparently not though, because he was rated #18 in the popularity poll. Who the hecks favorite character is abusive Akito? <br /><br />I think it’s fitting that Arisa is on the cover of a volume that mostly has Kyoko’s story in it, since they’re really similar. I could go off on a little rant about Arisa and Kureno and how it’s still weird, but also a little different than Kyoko and Katsuya, but I won’t right now. <br /><br />If I was to rate the first four chapters, it would probably be a two. I did enjoy the part with Tohru and Momiji watching back the school play, then making food, but I really can’t overlook the Age difference and abuse of power in Kyoko and Katsuya’s love story, even if Katsuya himself was a really great guy. I’m really sorry, but I just can’t. The last two chapters I would probably rate a four. Haha, I just realized that’s the opposite of the other rating. So overall my rating is a three. I wish I could rate it higher, sorry I can’t. Thank you for coming to my TED talk. <br /><br />Baby Tohru is adorable, obviously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6465758876794602648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2717751966?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani" href="/user/show/17978365-dani">Dani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2717751966&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2717751966" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11114306181811972329">I'm not crying, you're crying. I forgot how sad Kyoko's past was until reading this volume. It was interesting to learn that Kyo was privvy to such delicate information and learned all there was about Kyoko and how she had met Katsuya, Tohru's dad. I was straight up bawling because I could feel her pain and suffering when she thought she was alone in the world after Katsuya died and it made me wonder if I'll be like that if my husband were to leave me suddenly? I was also intrigued with how Kyok</span>
  <span id="freeText11114306181811972329" style="display:none">I'm not crying, you're crying. I forgot how sad Kyoko's past was until reading this volume. It was interesting to learn that Kyo was privvy to such delicate information and learned all there was about Kyoko and how she had met Katsuya, Tohru's dad. I was straight up bawling because I could feel her pain and suffering when she thought she was alone in the world after Katsuya died and it made me wonder if I'll be like that if my husband were to leave me suddenly? I was also intrigued with how Kyoko reacted when she found out she was pregnant and I think there are a lot of women who have the same question when presented with the knowledge of being a new parent, but the way that Katsuya answered her made me realize that so long as you have a loving partner like him, then you'll be able to set aside those fears and uncertainties.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer12627583&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer12627583" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10875978094676417128">I just finished reading this volume of Fruits Basket 3 hours ago. Surprisingly, I kinda liked this volume. I haven't read Furuba since last year, so I completely forgot the plot, the characters, and everything else. XD And I normally complain about Natsuki Takaya's drawing stlye- after she injured her drawing hand (during the seventh or eighth book, I think). <br/><br/>In a few parts of the book, I caught myself thinkking,"Hey, this image wasn't drawn so horribly...it kinds resembles her old drawing style</span>
  <span id="freeText10875978094676417128" style="display:none">I just finished reading this volume of Fruits Basket 3 hours ago. Surprisingly, I kinda liked this volume. I haven't read Furuba since last year, so I completely forgot the plot, the characters, and everything else. XD And I normally complain about Natsuki Takaya's drawing stlye- after she injured her drawing hand (during the seventh or eighth book, I think). <br /><br />In a few parts of the book, I caught myself thinkking,"Hey, this image wasn't drawn so horribly...it kinds resembles her old drawing style". And at the end of each chapter, I felt that the characters are developing a lot- it just kinda makes me feel happy.<br /><br />For instance: Yuki Sohma. I had always regarded him as the silent character that kept all his problems to himself and didn't open up to anyone, due to "problems" in his childhood. Yet in this volume, I find him laughing, joking and chatting with the other members of the student council, like Makeru Tanabe (I think that's his name, off the top of my head right now XD). He's even developed to the point where he's not just worrying about making friends himself- but caring for others (Machi). I thought,"The members of the studnet council form a very nice group, actually. They're kinda looking out for each other".<br /><br />The story of Tohru's mother and father was sad. They were such a great couple, but their marriage and happiness was, unfortunately, short-lived. Poor Tohru was only maybe 3 years old when her father passed away. --&gt;And it was from a freaking cold?!? How'd he die from a cold? XD<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10875978094676417128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2745994610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2745994610" />
    <a title="Ben Truong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77170844-ben-truong"><img alt="Ben Truong" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2745994610?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ben Truong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ben Truong" href="/user/show/77170844-ben-truong">Ben Truong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77170844-ben-truong?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2745994610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7153650325577503408"><i>Fruits Basket, Vol. 16</i> continues where the previous tankōbon left off and contains the next six chapters (90–95) of the on-going manga series.<br/><br/>Conflicted over his growing feelings for Tohru Honda and the approaching deadline for his confinement, Kyo Sohma also feels guilty for not telling her he knew her mother. He remembers when he was a boy, Kyoko Honda (then Katsunuma) told him about her past as a gang member, her meeting Katsuya Honda as a student teacher at her middle school, and falling in </span>
  <span id="freeText7153650325577503408" style="display:none"><i>Fruits Basket, Vol. 16</i> continues where the previous tankōbon left off and contains the next six chapters (90–95) of the on-going manga series.<br /><br />Conflicted over his growing feelings for Tohru Honda and the approaching deadline for his confinement, Kyo Sohma also feels guilty for not telling her he knew her mother. He remembers when he was a boy, Kyoko Honda (then Katsunuma) told him about her past as a gang member, her meeting Katsuya Honda as a student teacher at her middle school, and falling in love with and marrying him. How she gave birth to their daughter, whom Katsuya loved, but died shortly of pneumonia on a business trip, and in her grief she nearly killed herself before remembering that her toddler daughter needed her, which she concludes that we all need to be needed.<br /><br />After finishing all the work of the year the student counsel decide to celebrate by going out to dinner. In the way to their meeting place Yuki Sohma meets Machi Kuragi. When she falls her things are thrown on the floor, above her things Yuki finds a gift he gave to her which makes her blush and have a brief fight.<br /><br />At New Year's, Tohru and Kyo stays at Kyo's father who are surprised to find out Rin Sohma is staying too and that she has decided not to go to the celebration. At the New Year's zodiac banquet, when Akito Sohma tells Yuki he forgives his past transgressions, Yuki first tells Akito he forgives him, and then retracts, because it implies that there was some blame on Akito’s part. Akito strikes Yuki with a bottle before storming off. Meanwhile, Tohru asks Kyo what his New Year's wish would be this year, but he asks her to reveal hers as well in order to be fair. However, her wish is to break the curse, which she doesn't want him to know.<br /><br />This tankōbon is written and illustrated by Natsuki Takaya. For the most part, I really liked the direction of the narrative. The backstory of Kyo Sohma is further deepened and his connection to Tohru Honda is further deepened. It seems that the fates of the Sohmas particular those of Yuki Sohma and Kyo were intertwined with her family.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Fruits Basket, Vol. 16</i> is a wonderful continuation to a series that seems intriguing and I cannot wait to read more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7153650325577503408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3158622094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3158622094" />
    <a title="Fiona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21373198-fiona"><img alt="Fiona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373663367p2/21373198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3158622094?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fiona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fiona" href="/user/show/21373198-fiona">Fiona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3158622094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7575823483152853661">After fifteen volumes this is the first to feature Tohru's father and the story of how he met Kyoko. Although I'm generally not as bothered by age gaps in fiction or real life as other people are this is one example where it bothers me, mostly because Katsuya was a teacher and Kyoko was only fifteen when they met. I feel like if Kyoko had been out of school then it wouldn't have bothered me as much but the imbalance is pretty squicky for me, although otherwise they're pretty cute. <br/><br/>Outside of tha</span>
  <span id="freeText7575823483152853661" style="display:none">After fifteen volumes this is the first to feature Tohru's father and the story of how he met Kyoko. Although I'm generally not as bothered by age gaps in fiction or real life as other people are this is one example where it bothers me, mostly because Katsuya was a teacher and Kyoko was only fifteen when they met. I feel like if Kyoko had been out of school then it wouldn't have bothered me as much but the imbalance is pretty squicky for me, although otherwise they're pretty cute. <br /><br />Outside of that story and the mystery of just how Kyo met Kyoko to hear that story and why he seems to feel so much guilt around her death, especially with his feelings for Tohru, the most important part of this volume is Yuki going back to the Sohma house for the new year celebrations and confronting Akito. That's possibly not the right word though as he's able to let go of his anger for everything Akito's done to him. It's interesting seeing how Akito reacts to that and how unable they are to let go in the same way. It's a sign of progress for me in terms of breaking the curse, even though there's a long way to go.<br /><br />The other main development of this volume is the insight into Machi's character. So far she's mainly been in the background so it's great to start seeing things from her perspective. She's one of the few characters at the school who seems to see Yuki as he actually is beyond his good looks. Amongst fans she doesn't seem to be that popular, probably because of her awkwardness, but I find that refreshing in a series full of eccentric extroverts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7575823483152853661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luisa Maula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luisa Maula" href="/user/show/82149072-luisa-maula">Luisa Maula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82149072-luisa-maula?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3260428373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16600738770200339775">Looks like we’re there and back again at dealing with past traumas. The readers are given an insight with Kyoko’s backstory this time, which deals with heartache and betrayal, nothing like the mother of Tohru Honda we hear so much about. <br/><br/>Kyoko was a completely different person from her current self before losing her life to a car accident. She used to be as bad as Akito, belittling others and constantly gets into fights for the heck of it. <br/><br/>Kyoko sees herself a lot from Uotani due to having simil</span>
  <span id="freeText16600738770200339775" style="display:none">Looks like we’re there and back again at dealing with past traumas. The readers are given an insight with Kyoko’s backstory this time, which deals with heartache and betrayal, nothing like the mother of Tohru Honda we hear so much about. <br /><br />Kyoko was a completely different person from her current self before losing her life to a car accident. She used to be as bad as Akito, belittling others and constantly gets into fights for the heck of it. <br /><br />Kyoko sees herself a lot from Uotani due to having similar paths before. A gang member back then, disowned by their own families. If it weren’t for Kyoko’s change of heart, Tohru wouldn’t have been friends with Uotani at all. <br /><br />From this volume, it’s evident that having a family environment that lacks love and affection can potentially lead the child to ‘rebel.’ It’s that or they isolate themselves, thinking they’re unloved. Even so, that doesn’t mean they can’t get out of their situation. <br /><br />I like how the author gave an optimistic possibility that no matter how rotten you think you are, there’s always someone out there seeing the beauty in you. With that, hope comes to help you cope with your issues and before you know it, you’re a changed person. <br /><br />As for the other Sohma’s, I’m happy for Yuki to see’s he’s improved a lot compared to his past self. The way he’s shown friendliness to the introverted Machi made me ponder on that there might be something more on what their relationship holds as well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16600738770200339775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14064214015323228050" style="display:none">I'm getting less and less interested as each volume comes out. This one even less than the others.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U7bg4yU5+R+9UtoSk/H3ekuLAP2u250VJ0OHhskx8oo0qjJotIarLbZeYt1Cf+liZkbSyX1ndT6T/9YBy93vMQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5Ih3x1beejNn3zlDSJi1WTsOiqkh1wt4GN3z58IwM56DlKVMx2EoAWzTgYyZFqtBFsNYnfJr41OsYaJgwNwuJQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12343974891968613386"><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18983717._' rel='nofollow noopener'>高屋奈月</a><br/><br/>Natsuki Takaya (高屋 奈月 Takaya Natsuki, real name Naka Hatake) is the penname of a Japanese manga artist best-known for creating the series Fruits Basket. She was born on July 7, 1973; (Tanabata). Takaya is left-handed and once revealed that she wanted to be a mangaka since first grade, when her sister started drawing. <br/><br/>She was born in Shizuoka, Japan, but was raised i</span>
  <span id="freeText12343974891968613386" style="display:none"><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18983717._" rel="nofollow noopener">高屋奈月</a><br /><br />Natsuki Takaya (高屋 奈月 Takaya Natsuki, real name Naka Hatake) is the penname of a Japanese manga artist best-known for creating the series Fruits Basket. She was born on July 7, 1973; (Tanabata). Takaya is left-handed and once revealed that she wanted to be a mangaka since first grade, when her sister started drawing. <br /><br />She was born in Shizuoka, Japan, but was raised in Tokyo, where she made her debut in 1992. She enjoys video games such as the Final Fantasy series or Sakura Wars, or working on her different manga series, such as Fruits Basket, which is the second best-selling shōjo manga ever in Japan, and the top selling shōjo manga in North America. Fruits Basket has also been adapted into a twenty-six-episode anime series. <br /><br />In 2001, Takaya received a Kodansha Manga Award for shōjo manga for Fruits Basket.<br /><br />According to Takaya (in a sidebar of a Fruits Basket manga volume), she enjoys drawing girls (girly ones) more than she does boys. Takaya also enjoys electronics and music, but dislikes talking about herself. Also revealed in a sidebar of Fruits Basket, Takaya broke her drawing arm (left) after Fruits Basket volume six was published. She had to go into surgery, and as a result, had put Fruits Basket on a brief hiatus. Takaya made a full recovery, but complains that her handwriting had gotten uglier, due to the surgery. During her hospital stay, she gained an interest in baseball.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12343974891968613386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
